Indian Cotton Crop Feared to Be Quite Smooth

The market trend was quite firm last week due to the devaluation of the French franc, which sparked speculative interest. However, most transactions were speculative in nature. Before the U.S. cotton next government report is released, it may trigger long liquidation. Export inquiries are peaceful. Japan is buying new cotton. On the mainland side, interest is weak due to financial instability. The cotton harvest is generally smooth. Only the Broach cotton crop is slightly below the annual average. The attached statistics for last week are as follows (unit: 1,000 bales).

According to a Bombay telegram, the opening forecast on the 5th was: Broach 220 rupees, up 1 rupee; Oomra 198 rupees, up 1.5 rupees; Pingal 157 rupees, up 0.75 rupees.

Private US Cotton Estimates Reported Increase

A New York telegram dated the 3rd stated that the Pinnate Company's estimate for the current new cotton crop is 54.3% for production, with a yield of 11,331,000 bales, an increase of 151,000 bales compared to the previous estimate (August 29).

Three-Product Yarn and Cotton Prices Fluctuate in Osaka

An Osaka telegram dated the 5th stated that three-product futures yarn fell 6 cents to 1.80 yuan, with the near month at 213.60 yuan and the far month at 206 yuan. Futures cotton rose 10 cents to a drop of 6 cents, with the near month at 66.65 yuan and the far month at 66.30 yuan.

Piece Goods Spot Cotton Cloth Demand is Extremely Urgent Raw Materials, Yarn and Thread are Insufficient, and Factory Shipments are Greatly Reduced

Yesterday, the cotton cloth market strengthened as the situation eased slightly. Futures yarn and cotton rose sharply due to active spot sales, and the cotton cloth market also rose firmly. Eastern fine cloth and fine twill prices increased by 5 cents per piece. Local factory fine cloth and fine twill also rose by 5 to 10 cents. Light-weight coarse cloth and coarse twill sales were as usual, while heavy-weight coarse cloth and coarse twill were the most popular, rising by 10 to 20 cents per piece. The sales of fancy goods were similar to those at the end of last week, but spot goods became increasingly tight, due to the extremely urgent demand in the market and the insufficient supply of gray cloth and raw materials, yarn, and thread. Unbleached fine cloth and coarse cloth were also uniformly lacking in spot goods. For example, heavy-weight 16-pound coarse cloth originally had more than 20 brands to sell, but now it has been reduced to 6 or 7 brands, and spot goods are still being delivered sporadically. This shows the scarcity of production. Yesterday, the delivery of printed flannel, thread, and tribute drill was the most prosperous, all of which were goods dispatched by various factories on the same day. Although the market is gradually rising, new customer transactions are becoming increasingly active, and people's sentiment is very excited, especially in Sichuan, Yunnan, Fujian, and Guangdong.

Melton Market Condition Exceeds Flat Thick Cloth

The trend of Melton cloth has been getting better recently, and customers from near and far are making purchases. This is because 60-70% of military, government, and school uniforms are made of this cloth, but arrivals are thin and inventories are lacking. There is a strong sense that the market will get better as prices rise, and its trend has exceeded that of flat, thick cloth. Yesterday, high-end Melton cloth was sold in batches at 3.85 yuan per yard, and the lowest-grade, basic goods were sold in batches at 2.25 yuan per yard for the whole box.

Grains Tianjin Merchants Actively Purchase Flour, All Months See New Records

Yesterday in the flour market, prices in the morning showed an initial flat trend, followed by continued strong increases in all months. The quoted prices for foreign wheat in Chicago and Canada continued to be good, rising about 20 to 30 cents. However, when prices opened, people's sentiment was still stable. Then, because Tianjin flour sales were strong (with recent sales of 70,000 to 80,000 units), and prices were also rising, people's sentiment gradually improved and transactions became very active. The closing prices for each month of the week were up by 3 to 4 cents. When the market opened in the afternoon, the momentum became even more severe. January and February prices were all above 50 cents. The highest price for the March contract even reached 3.60 yuan (all months setting new records). Transactions were very active. After the closing, this month's prices were also high, at 35 and a half cents. However, as the upward trend became strong, large long positions closed positions for profit, so the market gradually calmed down. The current upward trend is mainly due to the initial active purchasing by Tianjin merchants, but ultimately it is still because foreign wheat is not easily accessible.

It is Said that the Wheat Market's Rising Trend is Not Yet Over

Yesterday, the futures wheat market opened in the morning with prices consistently firm across all months. Because foreign wheat quotations continued to improve by 20 to 30 cents, the market sentiment was stable. Opening prices for each month were better by 30 to 50 cents compared to the previous week. However, wheat trading outside the industry was relatively rare, so transactions were not very active. When the market opened in the afternoon, the improved flour market in the morning stimulated the industry's sentiment, and short positions were actively covered. Speculative clients from Beijing also followed suit and bought, and each month rose by 50 to 60 cents compared to the morning. The increase in each month was as high as 110 to 120 cents. Observing subsequent developments, the rising trend may not yet be over. In the spot wheat market, the price of extra high-quality wheat also increased by 10 cents, with Yingzhou Shandong wheat at 5.40 yuan, Hefei wheat at 5.20 yuan, second-grade at 5.19 yuan, Jiangbei wheat at 5.15 yuan, Wuhu wheat at 5.17 yuan, second-grade at 5.05 yuan, third-grade at 5.00 yuan, Huaian wheat at 5.25 yuan, second-grade at 5.20 yuan, Yanghe wheat at 5.35 yuan, second-grade at 5.32 yuan, Yaowan wheat at 5.29 yuan, Suqian wheat at 5.15 yuan, Gaoyou wheat at 5.20 yuan, Nanjing wheat at 5.10 yuan, Fuxin bought 7,000 packages, and Shenda sold 5,000 packages.

Demand for Ke Xian Rice Increases

Yesterday, less than 10,000 packages of newly arrived Ke Xian rice were available, but both this street and Shantou and Guangdong had keen demand. Total market transactions exceeded 25,000 packages. In addition, merchants in the producing areas were hoarding, and the number of shipments gradually decreased. River rice had already seen an increase, and foreign wheat was not cost-effective. Therefore, sellers had upward momentum and gradually raised prices. Yesterday, Benke actively purchased, and prices rose sharply by 10 to 20 cents. Guangdong continued to actively purchase brown Ke Xian rice, while Shantou and this street focused on machine-milled rice. North Ocean merchants also transacted a small number of foreign rice, 1,000 packages. Inland and Zhejiang merchants also made small purchases, so the market turned brisk. If Ke merchants continue to buy actively in the future, market prices may need to rise further. Throughout the day, 13,400 packages of Jiangxi rice, 5,200+ packages of Hunan rice, 5,000 packages of Shashi and Hankou brown rice, 660 packages of Zha Xian rice, and 1,000 packages of Xiaojiao rice were shipped.

Northern Merchants Purchase Seed Rice

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the sources from various merchants surged, with a total of nearly 50 firms arriving, carrying over 10,000 piculs of goods. The sales market on this street was also active, with purchases including over 1,000 packages of seed rice from Dalian, Qingdao, Weihaiwei, Qinhuangdao, and Yantai, as well as over 200 packages of thin and broken rice. Therefore, although the arrival of seed rice, Baige, and new glutinous rice was strong, they did not continue to fall, and the market was stable. However, white glutinous rice sales were weaker and fell by two cents, and Dujian rice, due to oversupply, depreciated by a small amount. Foreign glutinous rice remained unchanged. The sale of thick and thin broken rice slowed down at times, so prices fell again by 10 to 20 cents. Old and deteriorated original goods were rare and showed no profit or loss. New Yin Yuan rice was mediocre.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, 37-38 firms from the river arrived with various goods. Sales in the market were flat in the morning but improved in the afternoon. The market for broken and high-quality rice was stable, with medium and low-quality rice being slightly tight. High-quality new glutinous rice stood firm, while prices for medium and low-quality new glutinous rice increased by about 10 cents. The prices of new Yangdu and Bujian rice were slightly tight. Thin, early-season, deteriorated and original, and Ke glutinous rice showed no profit or loss. Sales were weak in the morning but tight in the evening.

Silk and Tea Overseas Silk Market Sees Another Turnaround

Yesterday there was no market in New York. Yokohama spot and forward goods rose by about 30-50 yuan. The Shanghai silk market seemed to be thinking of moving after a long period of quiet. Also, overseas silk prices have remained relatively stable. Therefore, yesterday, many telegrams were sent externally by local Western firms to reverse the situation. Whether this will happen will depend on tomorrow's New York market conditions. It is understood that the foreign purchase price for White Factory Brand characters seven and eight, with an even fineness of 0.22 strands, only fetched a price of 640-650 yuan. 13.15 strands fetched 680-690 yuan. However, the local market's usual price for the former is around 670 yuan, and the latter is around 720 yuan. Therefore, transactions were difficult. Yesterday, only Da Chang and other foreign firms made small purchases. Among users, the Hangzhou merchants made some transactions. Market sentiment and people's confidence were still stable, but transactions were quite slow.

New Arrival of Thin Iron Sheets

Thin iron sheets, which had been out of stock for many days, arrived at various warehouses such as Kung Ho Cheung, New Taikoo, etc., over the past two days (estimated to be three hundred twenty to thirty boxes). This has alleviated concerns about stock shortages in the market. The market price is 65 yuan per box. It is reported that fellow traders have already sold forty to fifty boxes, mainly purchased by cigarette companies and biscuit factories.

Fuzhou Line

Green Tea Transactions Still Scarce

Yesterday, green tea transactions by foreign firms remained scarce. British and French firms hesitated due to telegrams from Morocco indicating prices were too low and didn't align with current market prices. A wait-and-see attitude prevailed, and the market remained sluggish. Only a few firms like Xiehe purchased approximately 300 chests of Lu Zhuang "Zhen Mei" and "Zhen Zhen Mei" green tea, with prices falling by one or two yuan compared to previous sales.

North-South Goods: Why are Xiamen Tangerine Cakes Arriving Late? — Shantou Tangerine Cakes are Large and Beautiful —

Xiamen tangerine cakes have been in short supply due to inventory shortages in the producing areas, resulting in prolonged unavailability. It had been out of stock for a long time. It has been found that a small amount has arrived on the "Taiyuan" ship yesterday, and samples can be seen today. If the goods are bright red, they should sell well, but unfortunately, the goods have arrived too late. Otherwise, if they had arrived before the holidays, the prices could have been increased.

Tangerine cakes from Meishuitou are large, beautiful, and of excellent quality. Supplies are also scarce. Only five pieces arrived at the market a few days ago, which were sold yesterday, rising by one or two yuan compared to before.

Sugar Market: Guangdong Coarse White Sugar Transactions Weak

Yesterday, the sugar market trend was stable. The association's set price for coarse granulated white sugar was 21.8 yuan, and imported goods were 6.4 yuan. Only Dong Bai No. 8 spot goods rose by five cents, to 21.45 yuan, with no other changes. Mian Bai Zhen No. 1 from this factory was 20.5 yuan; the rest remained unchanged. The market saw the Chaozhou gang selling over a hundred bags of second-grade red sugar at 13.45 to 13.65 yuan, Yi Ji red sugar at 14.95 yuan, trading over forty bags, Zhiyang forty bags at 17.8 yuan, Nanjin green sugar several dozens of bags at 14.3 yuan, and ordinary Longxing over a hundred bags at 12.9 yuan.

The joint venture company held its first tender for Guangdong sugar this week, with a total quota of over ten thousand bags. Tender prices remained as before. The company sold 750 bags of Dechang's "Five Rams" coarse white sugar at 21.5 yuan, 70 bags from Jieyang Factory at 21.3 yuan, another 100 bags at 20.9 yuan, and 74 bags of granulated white sugar from the market at 19.4 yuan.

Hardware: Thick Tinplate Sales Robust

Thick tinplate sales have been exceptionally strong recently. It has been found that four to five hundred boxes were sold in the past few days. The best quality is priced at 100 yuan per box, the second best at 80 yuan, and the best "wild chicken" goods (i.e., those with uneven sizes) sell for 80 yuan, the second best for 60 yuan. In addition to the military's needs, yarn factories have also been stocking up on this product recently.

The Fate of Hair

— Han Ashe

Hair truly has a tumultuous fate. In medieval times, it was targeted and used in the "kun" punishment, which involved shaving the head completely bald.

After the abolition of the "kun" punishment, it managed to survive for several years. Monks and nuns don't count, but in the early Qing Dynasty, it suffered another misfortune when all hair was changed into queues and shaved off.

By the mid-Qing Dynasty, the Taiping Rebellion had lost a large part of the country. Their people never shaved their heads, so they were called "Longhairs." People at that time were in a very difficult position: shaving their heads meant death if they met the "Longhairs," and not shaving their heads meant death if they met the Qing soldiers. This was a time when "double hair" might have emerged.

After the Taiping Rebellion was quelled, the whole country uniformly dragged a pigtail behind their heads, and it seemed that hair would no longer be a problem. However, by the late Qing Dynasty, Western customs had spread to China, and people with vision knew that dragging this queue was shameful, but the national law did not allow you to cut it off. Even so, the motive for disaster had been planted. When the Wuchang Uprising started, the first thing they did wherever the righteous flag went was to cut off queues. It has been twenty-five years since then, and queues should have been completely cut off. But in reality, this is not the case. Even someone who had been a minor official in the Qing Dynasty for even a day would hide and keep a small queue on the top of his head, as a former loyalist. And there are also old folks in poor and remote areas who keep a pigtail, thinking that if the rites are lost, they should be sought in the countryside, and that the ancient ways are still in the world.

The styles of hair now, apart from women, are many: parted hair, flat hair, monk's head... It is always thought that hair can continue like this, and no longer cause problems. But who knows that with the evolution of human affairs, it still needs to be discussed, such as students and soldiers who have to shave their heads. The most ridiculous thing was that last summer, in more than a dozen counties up and down the Huai River in northern Jiangsu, the new Fifth Division checked the Baobians, and rumors spread that those with hair were suspected. So one told ten, and ten told a hundred. In a few days, the streets everywhere were shining brightly, all in the same mold. But in reality, there was no such thing at all. It's just adding some business to the barbershops.

The future fate of hair cannot be predicted, but it will probably not be very dull. It will change with the times.

Red Bean Rice Dumplings

— Wei Jing

It seems like it was more than twenty years ago, in the ×× River area, that 'Red Bean Rice Dumplings' were already quite famous. Red bean rice dumplings are made by mixing red beans with glutinous rice and wrapping them in rice dumpling leaves. However, the red bean rice dumplings in ×× River were valued for their maker, and the maker was known for her dumplings, which had quite a history.

Speaking of the origin of these red bean rice dumplings, it might have been as far back as thirty years ago. On the south bank of the ×× River lived a pitiful widow with three children, barely making ends meet. Because she had nothing to cook, she sold some red beans and glutinous rice, selling red bean rice dumplings. At that time, the widow was only twenty-seven or eight years old. Although not beautiful, she was quite attractive. At that time, the atmosphere in Shanghai was not as debauched as it is now, so when such a young woman selling rice dumplings was discovered in the market, everyone flocked to patronize her. Coincidentally, the widow had three red moles on her face, so everyone gave her a nickname, calling her "Red Bean Rice Dumpling."

Since her nickname became "Red Bean Rice Dumpling," her red bean rice dumplings became famous day by day, and business became better and better. After five or six years, she renovated the house and simply opened a snack shop. But the most popular item with customers was naturally red bean rice dumplings, because she had accumulated five or six years of experience and made red bean rice dumplings with a unique flavor. Although there were also frivolous customers who patronized her because the proprietress was known as "Red Bean Rice Dumpling," most customers were there because her rice dumplings had a unique flavor.

In more than twenty years, she not only relied on selling red bean rice dumplings to provide for her family, but also earned considerable farmland and houses. A few years ago, her eldest son, younger son, and son-in-law all gained some social status, so they forced her to give up the snack shop to enjoy her old age. Although she was reluctant, she finally gave in to the requests of her children and sold the shop, living a peaceful life as an old woman. But those who knew her history still secretly called her "Red Bean Rice Dumpling" behind her back when they saw her.

Yesterday, I happened to be passing by her new house and saw that her family was holding a funeral. Looking closely, under the epitaph "Lasting Example" written by a certain celebrity, three moles were clearly arranged on the deceased's face. This was tantamount to telling me that the red bean rice dumpling old woman, who had built her wealth from scratch, had passed away. But the impression of red bean rice dumplings will never be erased from my mind.

Swapping Phoenixes

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 7: Deep Brotherly Love Hides Letter, Pities Weak Sister; Heavy Poetic Air Reveals Shadows, Laughs at Poor Scholar

Menglan smiled and said, "Why am I unreasonable?" Youmei said, "You know what you mean by what you said. Do I need to explain it in detail? What do you mean by this? Could it be..." At this point, she blushed and suddenly stopped talking. It seemed as if she was about to smile, but before the smile could show, she pursed her lips and puffed out her cheeks. Menglan laughed and said, "Are you still taking my joke to heart?" Youmei laughed and said, "Who takes your words to heart? I'm just kidding with you. Besides, you're feeling sad right now. I wouldn't bear to find fault with you." When Menglan heard this, she just smiled and didn't say anything else. Since they had said this much, Youmei couldn't continue with the reason for her visit. After chatting about other things, she took her leave. However, in this way, Menglan felt a great emotion in her heart, thinking that her fate was far worse than Youmei's. She had such a civilized family, such a free environment, and such a healthy body. What could she compare to her? Because of this, she felt extremely uncomfortable, as if she was getting sick again. She stayed upstairs all day and didn't even show her face to her family. According to her own mood, she didn't want to go to school. But then she thought that Guochi must have sent a letter in the past few days. If the letter wasn't sent to her home, it would definitely be sent to the school. In three to five days, the letter would be safe in the mailroom. But if it was too long, she was afraid that the letter would fall into someone else's hands. Therefore, she reluctantly struggled and went to school again. Speaking of which, it was an extremely contradictory thing. According to Menglan's own expression, she didn't want to correspond with Zhang Guochi. But if she didn't receive Guochi's letter, she felt like something was missing in her heart. She couldn't explain this to herself. What was the reason? During this time of expectation, Guochi was able to live up to her expectations. He sent a letter to Menglan every week. In this situation, there was another strange thing, that was, even though he sent letters, when the two met on the road, they just glanced at each other from afar. When they got close, they still lowered their heads and walked past. On Guochi's side, Menglan didn't know what he meant. On Menglan's own side, she felt that a girl couldn't talk to a stranger without reason. Although there was only a difference of twenty years between 1920 and now, in recent China, it felt like two centuries had passed. The young people around the age of twenty today don't believe how closed off the social interactions between men and women were at that time. (81)

Beginning of Eyebrow Painting

— Zhao Tiefan

The matter of eyebrow painting, as seen in our old history, should be from the Biography of Zhang Chang in the Han Shu; "...Also painted eyebrows for his wife, and in Chang'an, Zhang Jingzhao was known as 'Eyebrow Fude'...", the record is the earliest. Liu Xi's Shi Ming; "Dai represents, it means to remove the eyebrows and replace them." The explanation is more detailed. Shi Wen Lei Ju; "The Han palace women swept green Dai to paint moth eyebrows." This shows that the custom of eyebrow painting originated in the Western Han Dynasty. Liu Xi trained Dai as a substitute, which is also based on the same sound and meaning, as in Shuowen Jiezi, training Tian as Dian, training Kao as the meaning of old age. Cui Bao's Gujin Zhu; "The Wei palace women liked to draw long eyebrows." Tang Li Yishan's Untitled Poem; "Long eyebrows can already be painted," Zhu Qingyu's poem on Yishi Zhang Shuibu; "How deep or shallow is the eyebrow painting in fashion?" It can be seen that the custom of eyebrow painting was transmitted to the Wei and Tang dynasties and had not yet declined. Zhu's phrase "deep or shallow eyebrow painting" refers to the depth of the Dai color. Song Zhu Yi's Yijue Liao Miscellaneous Records: "Today's women shave off their eyebrows and paint them with ink, which is an ancient method." Zhu thought that the Song people used ink to explain that the Han people used Dai. Kao Chu Ci; "Powder white Dai black," it can be seen that Dai is also black, and the Han and Song dynasties used it for eyebrow painting, which is no different. Since the Song Dynasty, although there are no frequent records about eyebrow painting, poets often use eyebrow painting, which is extremely ordinary. The custom of eyebrow painting is very popular in modern times, and it can also be inferred that the custom of eyebrow painting has never been cut off since the Song Dynasty.

Sago Palm

— Chen Tianci

Guangdong has a kind of sago palm (this tree grows in tropical areas), which is five or six zhang high, and its leaves are composed of many leaflets. The center of the trunk has pollen, which is reddish-yellow and can be used to make cakes.

However, Cantonese customs are often superstitious, because the branches and trunks of the sago palm go straight up without branches, which is said to symbolize a man's devotion. Therefore, whenever a woman has a husband and has an affair, she must pray in front of the sago palm (it is said that there is a god in this tree), and secretly tie the man's belt to the trunk, so that the man can be devoted to the woman and grow old together.

Therefore, every sago palm in Guangdong can often see many incense sticks, incantations, paper figures, and other sacrificial offerings, plastered all over the foot of the tree.

Miscellaneous Talks on Autumn Insects

— Cheng Xuan

The season of "Autumn Sounded by Insects" has come again! Indeed, whether in the morning or evening, in the city or the countryside, you can hear autumn insects singing tunes composed by nature everywhere. However, when sad people hear it, they not only don't enjoy the beauty of this song, but instead arouse their sorrows, like Ouyang Xiu's Autumn Sound Fu, "But I only hear the sound of insects chirping on all four walls, as if to assist my sighs!"

Among the autumn insects, the cricket is the most popular. Although it is autumn and dark, some people also support the cricket. Therefore, when it comes to autumn insects, scholars in the past have used crickets to arouse their literary interest and poetic inspiration, I don't know how much. Indeed, crickets are quite interesting. Its chirping sound, unlike other autumn insects, can be used as a thermometer. It is like the swallow among birds, a migratory bird that knows the time, predicting climate change. This is because its every move is related to climate temperature changes. In May, it can only jump, in June it can fly and chirp. By August, due to the invasion and attack of the cold, it moves from the wilderness to the foot of the wall for self-defense. By October, it comes to the bed to seek survival. I remember that a famous meteorologist Broc said that the most active period of crickets is from summer to mid-autumn. When the Fahrenheit thermometer is fifteen degrees, it is the lowest limit of cricket chirping. Broc went on to say that at Fahrenheit 79, it chirps 183 times per minute. When the temperature drops, the chirping also decreases, until it stops outside the temperature limit. Therefore, its chirping can be used as a thermometer, and it is very accurate! And if its chirping is clearer than usual, you can know that there are signs of a storm! When it comes to Chinese crickets, I feel that the greatness of its chirping is really not comparable to ordinary autumn insects!

Shen Bao Medical Special

Medical Examination

— Yao Xing Shu

Medical examinations are gradually attracting social attention. Patients need examinations, and healthy people also need examinations, called health examinations; in addition to one person being examined, there are also group examinations. No matter what, the effectiveness of medical examinations seems to be being elevated by someone every day. Although this is irrelevant to the value of the examination itself.

Usually, I observe that the general public has two views on examinations: one is that they overbelieve in examinations, bordering on superstition, and the other is that they do not believe in examinations, which is somewhat stubborn. These two opposite attitudes commit the fault of going too far.

Everyone should know that when new doctors diagnose illnesses, they use the methods of visual examination, tactile examination, percussion, and auscultation. This is using the innate abilities of the five senses to do some exploratory work on the patient's body, using it to help diagnose, in order to facilitate treatment. The method is simple, very practical, and can be said to be the beginning of medical examinations. However, the power of the five senses is limited, and sometimes it is not enough to meet our needs, which is also a fact.

Medicine is progressing every day, and other sciences are also becoming more prosperous day by day. Therefore, the methods of medical examinations are becoming more complex. They can be divided into three types: 1. Biological examinations, including various bacteria, microbial examinations, blood reactions, etc.; 2. Physical examinations, including blood pressure measurement, X-ray fluoroscopy, etc.; 3. Chemical examinations, including examination of sugars, proteins, gastric juice, etc. Although these have excellent equipment and meticulous methods, they have undeniable value; but the four methods of visual, tactile, percussion, and auscultation, which are regarded as the beginning of medical examinations, still maintain their arrogant posture. All pure doctors know that a pair of black eyes, two fleshy ears, and a pair of jade hands can gain something from the symptoms. In addition, our past experience can also greatly supplement the shortcomings of mechanized test tubes, microscopes, X-rays, etc.

We must understand that all examinations are only in a supporting position in medical treatment, and are only helpful for diagnosis and treatment. Those who are superstitious about it regard the auxiliary as the only one, which makes the examination feel flattered; those who do not believe in it regard the value of the auxiliary as worthless, which is too unfair to it. Originally, the results of the examination can only represent a part of the facts, and cannot reach the entirety of the facts. It should not be regarded as the entire report of each patient.

For example, people with pulmonary tuberculosis can detect tuberculosis bacteria in their sputum; people with purulent leucorrhea can detect gonorrhea in their secretions. If it is detected, it is ironclad evidence that the patient is indeed suffering from pulmonary tuberculosis or purulent leucorrhea. Isn't the examination enough for people to believe? But not being able to detect it is also common. We can only say that no tuberculosis bacteria were found in the sputum, and no gonorrhea were found in the secretions. We cannot say that this person does not have this disease. Therefore, the examination is not enough for people to believe. For example, whether or not there is syphilis, most people already know to solve it by testing blood, but in special circumstances, the blood reaction of syphilis patients cannot be detected; this does not mean that they do not have syphilis. When malaria attacks, malaria parasites can indeed be detected in the blood, but there are also many patients who cannot detect them, and we still have to regard them as malaria. In short, all examinations, such as not detecting anything, is not an absolute indication that there is no such disease.

To bring the conversation back, if something is detected in the examination, it seems reliable, but experienced doctors do not think that way. They still have to compare it with all the symptoms and study it carefully before making a diagnosis. This is the doctor's business, and there is no need to say more about it here.

In short, the results of medical examinations are affected by various environments. For example, a person with closed pulmonary tuberculosis (that is, the part of the lung disease does not communicate with the trachea) is not easy to find tuberculosis bacteria in the sputum; syphilis patients who have received incomplete syphilis treatment may not show a blood syphilis reaction. In addition, how is the technology and temperament of the person in charge of the examination work, which is related to the results of the examination. Therefore, not being able to detect anything, in addition to the factual difficulties, sometimes bears the responsibility of negligence; detecting something, sometimes bears the correct responsibility. Although these two responsibilities are not a problem legally; this makes the location occupied by the test even more visible.

Some Views on Promoting New Rural Medicine and Hygiene (Continued)

— Han Zhongying

(3) Utilizing the Baojia System—As mentioned above; relying solely on connecting with old doctors to promote new medicine and hygiene, while dealing with farmers who are like scattered sand, never having been subjected to the control of others, nor having experienced the suppression of others, thus developing a habit of lacking unity and organization, and lacking a consistent mind, and wanting to run to a rural area where one is unfamiliar and the organization is like scattered sand, to handle a perfect matter, is truly not an easy task! In the first half of the year, the government, in light of this, felt that the spirit of the farmers was too scattered and too unorganized, and held Baojia training. At the same time, those who were promoted to be Baojia chiefs were also outstanding figures among the farmers. Moreover, they had received a long period of proper training. It is much better to deal with them than with ordinary ignorant farmers because they are the leaders of the farmers, and they must be consulted on matters large and small. Therefore, for the promotion of new medicine and hygiene, it is necessary to first find a way to cooperate with them, which is no different from having ordinary farmers obey us, and saves a lot of trouble, while achieving satisfactory results in a simple way.

(4) To Make the Government and the People Cooperate—To popularize new rural medicine and hygiene, it is not enough to rely on a small amount of power. Therefore, the government and the people must cooperate. On the one hand, we should use the government's financial resources and influence to promote this work. On the other hand, we must rely on the masses to organize themselves automatically so that they can accept this work, striving for consistency between top and bottom, full cooperation, and jointly seeking the progress of this cause. Only then can this organizational work be effective and lasting; and new medicine and hygiene will have the hope of being promoted automatically.

(5) To Establish Free Clinics—To establish free clinics in the central locations of the countryside, because the provision of a little medical relief will arouse the "good feelings of the general farmers in the area where medical relief is provided for rural medical and health institutions." Regardless of the extent of the effect of this point on the effectiveness of rural medical and health treatment facilities; at the same time, when they come to the clinic, you can use some pictures, slogans, or impart some common knowledge of nursing for common diseases, pre-disease prevention, post-disease treatment, and daily life hygiene to them, so that they can understand the technology and value of new medicine, and know the relationship between the benefits and harms of hygiene and unhygienic conditions. This not only builds a solid foundation for new medicine, but also greatly helps to popularize rural medicine and hygiene.

(6) Training Personnel—Even with a sound organization and complete facilities, the lack of adequate staff is still an imperfection. In other words, it is a basic difficulty in promoting rural medicine and hygiene. Therefore, once the goals are determined, staff must be trained. According to the stipulated organization, you can know what kind of talents are needed, and then train such talents according to this need, so that supply and demand can be effectively matched, and the application of talents can also be appropriate. However, in terms of technical training, in addition to being fully based on scientific medical methods and knowledge, special attention must be paid to the cultivation of personality. This is the most easily overlooked thing in ordinary training of personnel. Regarding personality training, attention should be paid to the following points:

(1) Cultivate the spirit of "serving as the purpose." (2) Train in a simple life; it is necessary to ensure that the staff's life is almost the same as the life of the local people, so that the farmers do not feel a "disparity"; if the standard of living can be reduced, the salary will naturally not be high, and about thirty to forty yuan per month will be enough to satisfy. (3) Treat people with "sincerity" and be "faithful" in doing things! (4) Absolutely correct bad habits such as perfunctoriness, emphasis on appearances, laziness, lack of progress, perfunctory performance, and deception.

Finally, I have one more opinion to contribute to the current staff engaged in rural medicine and hygiene. It is very important that this kind of work can be promoted together by the entire society. At the same time, regarding the cause of rural revitalization, start by promoting rural medicine and hygiene and lay the foundation for rural revitalization; however, the degree of promotion in the future depends on whether we have a whole goal, a sound organization, and work hard and cautiously to complete this rural mission, which will not only provide security for farmers, but also greatly help the work of rural revitalization.

(1) Improving Education—Farmers live in remote villages, far from the city, and the education system is still the old method. They still read ancient books. As for what secondary education and higher education are, they do not even have the opportunity to enjoy primary education. People are not knowledgeable, and medicine and hygiene are naturally difficult to promote. Therefore, it is hoped that the pioneers in running rural medicine and hygiene and the leaders in the education field will do their best to promote new education and jointly seek the popularization and improvement of new rural education. The hygiene course can be listed as a basic course because hygiene education is the fundamental education related to national survival. Simple words can be used to teach them the causes of diseases, the prevention of diseases, the benefits of new medicine and hygiene, first aid treatments, and some unreliable knowledge such as praying to gods and asking divination, so that they can plant simple medical knowledge and hygiene concepts when they are young; for older people, teach them some new scientific knowledge and new living habits to open up their minds. In this way, a new rural area can be created in a few years, and at the same time, it will greatly assist in the promotion of new medicine and hygiene.

(2) Connecting with Old Doctors—Farmers cannot get the cultivation of new education, let alone the enjoyment of new medicine. In addition to seeking gods and asking divination, people who are relatively knowledgeable or wealthy all adopt old doctors and deeply believe in old doctors. There is no influence or concept of new doctors at all. Therefore, the general corrupt old doctors often persuade people to take out a medical package. The medicines they use are mostly some ascending and descending medicines, or some symptomatic medicines, just perfunctorily doing things. Therefore, the general ignorant farmers are poisoned by it, thinking that only doctors who offer a package of treatments can do their best to diagnose and treat, and use more good medicines. This is a common wrong concept of farmers; so-called doctors have a compassionate heart, how can they not diagnose and treat with all their heart. Moreover, new doctors do not offer a package of treatments, and at the same time, packages of treatments are prohibited by law. In addition, the nature of farmers is mostly stubborn, which is a major obstacle to the promotion of new doctors. Therefore, for new medicine and hygiene to be promoted without obstacles, it is necessary to connect with old doctors, stand on the same battle line, cooperate in research, and jointly seek the popularization and promotion of new medicine and hygiene. (The End)

Describing Li Kejia and Li Kejia's Illness (II)

— Chen Duanbai

Local Exanthematous Typhus Rndemischer Elethty dhus

Tsutsugamushi Disease Uberschezsfieber Saelz Tautsuzanussyi-Kraukheeit, T.fever Li Shizhen's Compendium of Materia Medica has the following records under the article on sand fleas:

Compendium of Materia Medica of Sand (Explanation of Names) Xuan Sound Geng Xuan Guangya Peng Huo Wanbi Technique

Land brand

Collection and Explanation Shizhen said, according to Guo Yigong's Guangzhi, sand fleas are in the water, red in color, no larger than a machine, entering people's skin, killing people. Wan Hong's Baopuzi said that fleas are found in both water and land, and after rain, in the morning and evening, stepping on sand will definitely attach to people like hairs pricking people, entering the skin, and can be picked out with a needle. It is as red as cinnabar. If not picked out, it will enter the flesh and can kill people. Whenever you encounter this flea, you should walk back and forth with fire to bake your body, and it will come out, following the fire. Also, Zhouhou Fang said that there are many sand fleas in the mountains and waters, which are very small and barely visible. When people enter the water or walk in the grass in the shade, these insects often attach to people and drill into the skin, causing people's skin to feel like being pierced by awn needles, red like millet beans. After three days of piercing, cold and heat cause sores, and the insects gradually enter the bones, killing people. People in Lingnan initially had this, and scraped it off with thatch leaves or bamboo leaves, and then applied bitter lettuce juice. If it is deep, pick it out with a needle, and the insects are just like scabies insects. I think that the poison of creek poison, the poison of shooting workers, and the poison of sand fleas are all similar, and all seem like typhoid fever, so there are methods of picking sand and scraping sand. Now, people who are sick with wind and cold scrape their whole body with hemp and peach and willow branches, which is also called scraping sand, which originated from scraping sand disease. Sand disease is also called water sand, water typhoid fever. In the beginning, it is like typhoid fever, headache, strong cooked nausea, slight coldness in the end of hands and feet, or abdominal pain and confusion, killing people in a moment, which is called twisting intestine sand.

Appendix, Shizhen said, according to Luyi Ji, there are sand insects in Tan Yuan Chu Ji and other states, which are poisonous snakes. The insects in the scales and shells are tormented. Every time they enter the rapids and are crushed out, people are poisoned by them and die in three days. This is also the amount of sand fleas.

Carefully reading the records proves that the vector of tsutsugamushi disease is the red mite Aka.muslin (scientific name Trombioua Akamushi). Its symptoms are similar to typhoid fever, so I dare to add a question mark to the term water typhoid fever and list it as a synonym for tsutsugamushi disease. Kawamura Rin'ya, a Japanese researcher of tsutsugamushi disease, also mentioned in his book "Research on Tsutsugamushi Disease" that this disease was also prevalent in the Xiangjiang and Ganjiang River basins in ancient China. He did not mention where his research came from, but I am afraid that it is not unrelated to the Compendium of Materia Medica mentioned above. Furthermore, based on our current situation, we cannot conclude that this disease has become extinct just because there are no reports from relevant parties (such as church hospital doctors). Li Kejia's research methods and paths are still in their infancy. The fact that typhoid-like diseases are confused with paratyphoid fever or similar symptoms is even a must-have fact in the current medical field. Regarding this disease, there is still room for discussion and necessity as to whether it actually exists within our country.

Common Knowledge Q&A on Diseases

— Cheng Hanzhang

(92) Gout (Bottom)

What is the prognosis of gout, good or bad?

If reasonable treatment can be carried out, it can be completely cured. If it is combined with kidney or heart disease, uremia or even stroke may occur, which is dangerous. Is it easy to diagnose gout?

Gout is easy to diagnose when it occurs, but it should be distinguished from acute rheumatic stiffness. Usually, it should be distinguished from chronic multiple arthritis or degenerative arthritis. How should gout be treated?

The treatment of gout should be carried out from three aspects: food therapy, drug therapy, and physical therapy.

What is food therapy?

The first priority of food is to prohibit eating meat and drinking alcohol. You can eat more plant-based foods such as fruits and vegetables. Milk, coffee, eggs, tea, mineral spring juice can all be used as much as possible. What is drug therapy?

Taking Atophan internally is the most effective, or using Atophan Neil injection. In addition, internal administration of salicylic acid can also be used. Analgesics should only be used temporarily. What is physical therapy?

In order to promote metabolism, exercise and warm baths should be carried out regularly. During acute attacks, wrap the joints and rest quietly in bed until the inflammation subsides before operating again.

Investigation Report on the Health Status of Haining Xiashi, Zhejiang (III)

— Shen Songnian

Among the public entertainment venues, the most elegant is the People's Education Hall, followed by the public sports field at the foot of Jue Shen Mountain, and then the Xiashi Theater, which is currently performing Peking Opera. The Xixi Park of the Tie Lu Labor at the foot of Zihui Mountain has long been corrupt and unbearable due to poor management; it is not as good as the Shen Garden outside Henggang Bridge, with its exquisite pavilions, flowers, and lush trees and bamboos, and its serene scenery. Famous products such as honey peaches and white orchids have long been well-known. The garden is quite tidy everywhere, and is most suitable as a public recreation place, but it is a private garden and rarely open, so the average public cannot feast their eyes.

(7) Charitable Organizations

The charitable organizations in Xiashi Town with slightly larger scale buildings are the Nursery, the Poor Children's Home, the Poor People's Skills Training Center, and the Homeless Shelter. There are more than ten names set up by other industries and philanthropists, but they often cannot be fully developed due to financial constraints.

(8) Produced Drugs

There are no special drugs here, and the produced drugs cannot be used for formal medical purposes because the farmland is mainly used for broad beans, rice and wheat, and there are no formal planting drugs. However, there are many names of drugs produced in uncultivated land, such as mountains, etc. The main ones are described as follows: Jingjie, Banbangzi, Taoren, Pyrethrum, Wild Chrysanthemum, Haijinsha, Digupi, Mint, Patchouli, Loquat Leaves, Apricot Kernels, Xiangyuan, etc.

(9) Small-Scale Factories

There are no large-scale factories in Xiashi Town. The electric light company can hold the bull's ear of Xiashi factories, followed by Kangtai, Tailong, Taifeng, Wanyouyu, etc., more than ten rice mills. Most of the workers are from Jiangbei because Jiangbei people can endure hardship and are loyal to their duties, and their wages are relatively low, so each factory is happy to hire them. As for health facilities, there are many areas for improvement.

(10) Endemic Diseases

There are no special endemic diseases in Xiashi, but beriberi (commonly known as Hong Kong foot) is very common. Since the domestically produced "Minsheng" cure-all ointment came out, the public can all treat themselves, so the sales of this "cure-all" are very good.

(11) Epidemics

In addition to the fact that the legally defined acute infectious disease plague has never been epidemic here, cholera, cerebrospinal meningitis, etc. have all been epidemic, but not very severely. This has to be attributed to the strict prevention and control of the authorities and medical institutions.

(12) Public Medical Institutions

(A) Anti-Smoking Center

The district-run anti-smoking center was ordered to open last October. The director is Chen Yuren, director of the Xiashi Public Security Bureau, and the deputy is Wu Guanlan, who is also the district chief. There are two doctors, one county-appointed doctor, one assistant doctor, two officers, and two workers. The smoking cessation method adopted is the foaming method and the morphine addiction reduction method, which has achieved remarkable results and has been praised by the superiors. Special Commissioner Wu Wangji praised it and said: It is the most effective among the nearby counties. No less than 300 people have quit and left the center. The required expenses are 300 yuan per month, and the source of funding is mostly raised by local gentry.

Hygiene Knowledge of Ear, Nose, Throat and Eye Diseases

— Tang Renjin

(102) What is night blindness and day blindness?

Our eyes have a function of distinguishing between light and dark. This function is called light perception in medicine. The rods in the retinal visual cells are dedicated to light perception. As for the cones, they are responsible for vision and color perception. The central part of the retina has more cones, and the edge part has fewer rods. Therefore, our ability to sense weak light is strongest in the edge part. There is also the so-called dark adaptation, which is when we enter a dark room from outdoors, we often cannot see everything in the room. After a moment, and after adapting to the darkness, we can clearly recognize everything in the room. Conversely, after staying in a dark room for a long time, when we suddenly go outdoors, we feel dizzy. But soon we can adapt to it and return to the original normal state. This situation is called light adaptation.

If light perception is weakened, or dark adaptation is impaired, it is specifically called night blindness in medicine. In short, the vision during the day is no different from ordinary people, but at dusk, or in places with insufficient light, the vision can be extremely reduced. Therefore, there are special names in the common people, such as sparrow eyes and chicken blindness (this is because the eyes of sparrows and chickens are also dim in the evening and bright in the morning.)

There are two types of night blindness, congenital and acquired. Acquired night blindness is further divided into two types: idiopathic night blindness and night blindness caused by organic changes in the retina.

(1) Congenital night blindness—For example, it often occurs in Oguchi's disease and white spot retinitis. Oguchi's disease was discovered by Japanese Oguchi Chuta. It is a congenital retinal abnormality. Children often complain of night blindness. White spot retinitis is a congenital degeneration of the outer layer of the retina. Scattered small white spots occur on the retinal surface. Among the subjective symptoms, night blindness is often complained of.

(2) Idiopathic night blindness—This disease is generally caused by malnutrition and lack of vitamin A. It is often accompanied by conjunctival xerosis. It is more common in poor children. It is easy to occur in summer and autumn. The body is often weak. The so-called sparrow eye and dry eye in the common people refers to this disease. The patient's vision is normal during the day, but he cannot see objects at dusk. This disease should be treated with more nourishment and internal administration of cod liver oil, which should have a miraculous effect. In ancient Chinese prescriptions for sparrow eye and dry eye, chicken liver, pig liver, beef liver, and sheep liver are often used. It is said that they are indeed effective. Therefore, the liver has indeed had a clear therapeutic value for this disease for a long time.

(3) Night blindness caused by retinal degeneration or atrophy—For example, it often occurs in retinal pigmentary degeneration and congenital syphilitic retinochoroidal atrophy. Retinal pigmentary degeneration is a hereditary disease. The descendants of consanguineous marriages are prone to suffer. At the same time, there are often systemic developmental disorders, deafness, or endocrine abnormalities. Usually both eyes are affected at the same time. Its main complaint is night blindness. Patients with congenital syphilitic retinochoroidal atrophy feel night blindness in childhood.

Day blindness is the opposite of night blindness. That is, the patient's vision is reduced in strong light. If it is in a slightly darker place, the vision can be improved. This can often be seen in axial optic neuritis and achromatopsia.

Shen Bao This City Supplement

Talk

Labor Diet Survey

— Meng Ruo

The life of workers is the most difficult. It is very appropriate to use the four words "cattle and horse life" as a metaphor. They work hard day and night, selling their blood and sweat, and the price they get is very meager, almost insufficient to maintain a basic life. Not to mention anything else, just in terms of diet, it is fortunate to not be hungry, where can we talk about nutrition?

According to a recent report from the Chinese Medical Association, an investigation was conducted on the diets of workers and their families in seven factories in Shanghai. The results found that the diet of child laborers was below the standard required limit in terms of both quality and quantity, and was worse than the diet of other workers. Also, the diet of workers is too high in carbohydrates, and the content of animal fat and animal protein is insufficient, and the quality is poor, which shows malnutrition.

People say, "Labor is sacred," which is certainly true. But when we see the living conditions of workers, we cannot help but feel chilled. The contribution of workers cannot be said to be small, but they live a hard life, or even worse than cattle and horses. Cattle and horses can hope to be full, but workers cannot get the minimum diet. Especially child laborers, who are in the process of development, their diet is worse than other workers. This can directly affect the health of workers and indirectly affect the efficiency of work.

Recently, we often hear people advocating "protecting workers," but to protect workers, the most important thing is to improve the lives of workers. The improvement mentioned here does not expect comfort, but only asks that they not be frozen or starved. But just this request may be difficult to achieve. Capitalists are always trying to find ways to carry out endless exploitation. They only see their own interests and do not care about the lives of workers.

The survey report of the Chinese Medical Association focuses on the diet of workers, which is related to physiology and hygiene and can be used for medical research, but it can also be used as a reference for those who care about the lives of workers. However, there are many aspects of the lives of workers that deserve attention. If we can conduct investigations in all aspects, it will be of great help to the improvement of workers' lives.

Setting Out

— Zhi Fu

——A New Compilation of Old History——

The north wind, which had been blowing continuously for three days, had stopped a large troop of soldiers entirely in the Huajiacun area, waiting for the storm to cease before they could break camp and set off.

This time, the battalion was preparing to be deployed to the Heishuitou area to be stationed. The day before the army set off, the battalion dispatched many soldiers to conscript able-bodied men to accompany them, even going to the villages to urge them from house to house.

Mulan—a young woman from Huajiacun—was sitting idly at home this day, her brow furrowed tightly, as if she had some difficult matter to resolve, sighing endlessly.

The surrounding air was very quiet. Suddenly, the sound of a horse bell approached from afar, and then someone knocked on her door.

"Who is it?" she asked outwards.

Page 18

"We are from the military camp to deliver a message," a rough voice answered from outside the door.

Mulan opened the door without hesitation, and she immediately saw the thick-browed man handing in the military conscription notice. His expression seemed very uneasy.

"The main force will set off at noon tomorrow. Your old man Hua has to return to the ranks too! If he is too old, then your brothers should go to assemble on time, without fail!" the soldier said a few words, hastily mounted his saddle, and galloped towards the hillside like a flying arrow.

"Alas!" Mulan sighed again, as if with some emotion, and immediately turned and ran inside. Inside, her parents hobbled out of the bedroom.

"Mulan! Who was that?"

"It was someone from the army," she said, handing the military conscription notice to her father to see.

Her mother looked at the old man's trembling wrist with frightened eyes, her eyes almost red and swollen.

"Dad! The man just now said we have to prepare to return to the ranks. I don't think you need to worry, this is for our entire country! At this critical moment of survival, the people should naturally take on their respective responsibilities. Now I have decided to disguise myself as an able-bodied man from the Hua family to follow the army on its expedition…"

She spoke with a face full of excitement, her willow-leaf eyebrows standing upright, and a bright flush appearing on her cheeks.

"You, you're crazy! How can a daughter…" her mother seemed even more panicked, trying desperately to stop her with a tearful face.

"…Who says a daughter can't shoulder a great mission! I, Mulan, am determined."

"There are many bad people in the army! You…" her father almost cried: …his throat felt like it was choked by an iron cake.

Mulan, however, was thinking about the preparations for the expedition. She secretly ran out of the house again and went to the market to choose a sturdy white horse, as well as bows, spears, saddles… and brought them back.

After half a day of careful disguise, Mulan came out of the bedroom, already transformed into a brave and martial man. Her younger brother looked at her and shouted wildly:

"Ah! Sister has changed her appearance! She's actually my brother now!"

Even her parents couldn't tell the difference at this time. He stared at her with his dim old eyes and suddenly laughed. However, when he thought that his beloved daughter would soon leave his side, a wave of bitterness welled up in his heart, and two streams of tears rolled down his cheeks.

"Dad! Why are you heartbroken?…" Mulan said heroically.

"My family is well, why do we have to… separate like this… uh!…" Her parents hugged her arms and cried loudly.

"What are you saying! Now that our country is about to fall, what kind of home do we have? We must do our best to drive away those barbarians, and when your daughter returns with a bloodstained sword, we will rebuild our sacred and harmonious family…!"

Mulan struggled to break free from her parents' embrace.

The two bitter hearts of the elderly were moved to stop crying. On one side, they hurriedly prepared to pack the remaining luggage for their daughter.

A heavy mist pressed down, and the fields of the village were shrouded in darkness. The wind seemed to have stopped as well. A clear whistle sounded in the distance, and the campfire illuminated the hillside in red. It was during this night that Mulan finally mounted her saddle and galloped away without looking back. …

Her parents leaned against the door of their home, watching their beloved daughter embark on a long expedition with tears in their eyes.

Wind

— Zheng Mingzi

The wind is cold and fluttering.

The fields began to become desolate: the rice stalks all turned yellow, and the leaves sparsely left the withered branches, falling to the ground, where passersby trampled them. In this way, they slowly rotted in the soil and disappeared. No one remembers them anymore, no one remembers the thick shade of summer! Now, the branches are bare, and there is no more laughter in the square at night. The fields are gradually becoming desolate: it is autumn.

The wind blows and blows, blowing the wilderness out of shape: when the season of withering arrives, nothing can escape its decline. The branches gradually become bare and withered, and even the two or three small blades of grass growing by the cracks in the stones wither and turn yellow…

Just as the old woman Ma in Jinjiazhen couldn't understand the hardships that this "remote corner of the world" had suffered over the years: "What exactly is going on, what evil wind has been encountered?…"

The old woman Ma's family had lived in Jinjiacun for at least eighty years, according to her own careful calculation on her fingers. It is said that she was brought here by her ancestors during the Taiping Rebellion, when the old woman Ma was only a six-month-old baby.

The family settled here, worked, and multiplied, and the days passed like that. The elderly died generation after generation, lying in the soil that their blood and sweat had irrigated, and now—according to calculations, the old woman Ma should even have great-grandchildren, and soon, perhaps, she would follow generations of ancestors and lie in the soil—however, now the old woman Ma has nothing. Her only son, nearly fifty years old, had his temperament ruined by poverty and anxiety. Every day he drank alcohol, and he never treated her with a kind voice again. "I'm about to die, and I still have to live that kind of life! What a sin, what a sin, what evil wind has been encountered…?"

It really seemed like they had encountered some "evil wind." The old woman Ma, who had lived for more than seventy years, had never lived through such days. In the past—even five years ago—life was much better. Her son worked in a yarn factory in Shanghai, and that year he became a "foreman," earning an extra five yuan in wages. When he returned home for the New Year, he even brought a young woman back, urging the old woman Ma to call her mother-in-law…

This time, the old woman Ma smiled happily. Her son had earned more money and gained a daughter-in-law. The whole family was happy. The days were getting better and better, really, it was like a peaceful world.

This small Jinjiacun was like a paradise isolated from the ugly world. Life was simple, and the days were light…

But at the end of the second year, before it was time to go home for the New Year, her son and daughter-in-law, who were working in Shanghai, both rushed back; saying that the ×× people were attacking Shanghai, the factory had stopped work, and Shanghai was in a panic.

However, "Shanghai" seemed so far away. The old woman Ma often heard her son talk about "Shanghai," which was a good place, but it shouldn't have had much to do with the remote Jinjiacun.

But, after four consecutive months, they also became anxious. It wasn't just the old woman Ma's family whose men were working in Shanghai in Jinjiacun. But sitting at home and eating away at their savings, they all couldn't hold out. In the fifth month, they hurriedly went to Shanghai to take a look: many shops and factories were no longer open, and even those that were open had reduced wages a lot. Speaking of the old woman Ma's son, he returned to his hometown three months after work resumed, saying that the factory had closed down. This time, there was nothing to do, and he had to stay at home.

In this way, the days became more and more difficult, and there was no way out. Losing his job, everything went wrong. Finding work again was harder than climbing to the sky. The old woman Ma's son immersed himself in alcohol every day. After getting drunk, he came back and scolded his old mother and beat his wife. The woman couldn't bear the torment, and in the third year, she quietly slipped away, leaving the helpless people in Jinjiacun living a miserable life like stray dogs: hunger, poverty, and misery…

"What evil wind is this!" The old woman Ma still couldn't understand: however, the world was indeed falling into a season of withering…

Little Master

—

Old拉克 and蕊莎

— Lin Na

拉克 returned from the royal city by carriage. He sat on the carriage platform, his eyes slightly closed, a pipe clenched in his mouth, appearing deep in thought. Behind him, the sunset glow was reflected in the long row of palm trees raising dust.

The old man was very depressed; he was thinking of home. Three years ago, there were his wife, two sons, and a daughter at home. Three years later, the situation had changed. His wife had died, his two sons had joined the Dan Niu Lan (peasant violent party) uprising, one was sentenced to permanent imprisonment, and one was in exile. Now, the only people left at home were the old man and his daughter, who was eighteen or nineteen years old. According to the habits of ordinary Filipinos, she could freely fall in love or marry, and he would have someone to rely on for the rest of his life. His daughter and son-in-law would be responsible for taking care of him in his old age, although he was confident that his muscles and bones were still strong enough to transport property from the small town to Manila, and he could also drive foreign goods from Manila back to the mountain shops in the countryside.

However, his daughter was so timid and indecisive since she was little. She grew up in the owner's coconut grove, and she didn't have the activeness and playfulness of ordinary girls. Many girls of her age were already walking with protruding bellies, but she hadn't even found a lover. Once, she was chased out of the coconut grove by the pursuers' love songs, her face red and ears burning, hiding in the house and crying; once, she poured a whole basin of cold water on the young singer who was serenading her under the window. It was just because she was afraid, afraid of those men and the lewd songs coming from their throats.

This made the old father very anxious. He believed that she would never get a lover because the young people in the village were afraid to approach her. (To be continued)

The strong bully the weak. You must fight and not be cowardly. Willing to love the community and the country as one. If you want a rich country and a strong people, you must rely on a good conscience. Young people are busy. Studying hard. Old people are busy. Achieving a career. The older you get, the stronger you get. The predecessors planted trees, and the descendants enjoy the shade. Compatriots share. What's the harm in being busy?

Movies

Introducing "Carnival Night"

We dare to, with the most sincere attitude, recommend this Chinese film, a glorious work of the world, "Carnival Night" to the ladies and gentlemen who love film art.

"Carnival Night" is a work that shows the progress of Chinese films, and is a work that improves the technical level. Although we dare not say that it is unprecedented, we are very confident that after you watch it, you will definitely be pleasantly surprised and praise it as an exquisite work.

Whether it is in terms of consciousness, director's skills, photography, scenery, actors, sound recording and sound effects, or the sentences in the dialogue, there are considerable and satisfactory gains. Of course, these satisfactory gains are the crystallization of huge assets and the hard work of all the staff, but in order to give the audience spiritually beneficial food, we have never taken into account the consumption of all our money and effort.

This film is now scheduled to be released on October 8 at the Jincheng Grand Theater in this city.

The Great Shanghai Will Screen "Queen's Martyrdom"

The Great Shanghai Grand Theater will screen the great palace film "Queen's Martyrdom" by RKO Pictures around National Day. The film stars Katharine Hepburn and Fredric March, and is directed by John Ford. It tells the touching story of the life of Mary, Queen of Scots. Mary suffered misfortune in her childhood and lived in France. When she grew up, she was betrothed to the King of France as queen, but before long, the King of France suddenly died. Therefore, she had a strong desire to return home. Queen Elizabeth of England heard the news and tried to stop her in every way, but Mary finally arrived safely in her homeland in a lone boat. After returning to the country, the ministers rebelled and the siblings quarreled. Fortunately, she met Earl Bothwell, who was sincere and loyal, and her heart was slightly comforted. However, due to political reasons, she had to marry Duke Darnley. At that time, the ministers used the power of the Queen of England to conspire to rebel. Mary's secretary, Riccio, was assassinated, and Duke Darnley died in misfortune. Mary then married Earl Bothwell, but as the siege became more urgent, she had no choice but to make an alliance with the rebels and say goodbye to the Earl. Later, she was deceived and forced to abdicate to the Crown Prince. As the Queen, she was reduced to a prisoner of the steps. In prison, she tried to seek help from Elizabeth, so that she could safely arrive in England. She thought that the light would be seen again, and that she could enjoy her years from now on. Unexpectedly, the Queen of England was unpredictable and imprisoned Mary again, and sentenced Mary to death for the heinous crime of plotting to take the Queen of England's life. On the day of the verdict, Mary initially denounced the Queen of England's conspiracy, but when she learned that Earl Bothwell had died in exile, she thought that she was alone and had no interest in living alone, so all her thoughts were gone, and she calmly faced her death. The joys and sorrows in the film are really touching. The people at sea should not miss this extraordinary historical palace film.

Casual Talk about the Double Xia

— Star

The Hebei opera in Shanghai now can be said to be at its peak, and the first people to introduce it to Shanghai, giving the general audience a good impression and gaining praise from all walks of life, are the sisters Zhu Baoxia and Zhu Zixia. Their skills can really be said to be perfect and have reached the realm of transformation. Zixia is good at playing young women, but is also proficient in young men. Baoxia, in addition to playing young women and huadan, is also good at leather flute and acrobatic martial arts. Her tone is sweet and rich, not inferior to Yushuang. She can be called the pride of Ping opera. Recently, Guan Jun, a famous playwright, specially arranged the play "Fox Fairy Fate" for the Zhu sisters. The performance was a great success, unprecedented. The play was performed for twelve days in a row, and every show was full, setting the record for the Yongji Great World and the Ping Opera Theater. It is now known that the Zhu sisters will continue to perform new plays in the coming days. The name of the play is "Qiankun Fushou Mirror". It is still written by the famous master Guan Jun. The scenes are compact, the matching is appropriate, and the Bouncing, Leather Flute, Qin Opera, and Gao Bozi are integrated into one. There is also a long joint performance. The tunes are novel and the words are elegant. Compared to "Fox Fairy Fate", it is even more exciting, and the Zhu sisters are also rushing to make new costumes for this play. The future of Ping opera will surely shine again. On the left is Zhu Baoxia's costume from the play "Fox Fairy Edge".
